<s> esmond's scheme his first visit was to bruxelles passing by way of antwerp where the duke of marlborough was in exile and in the first named place harry found his dear young benedict the married man who appeared to be rather out of humor with his matrimonial chain and clogged with the obstinate embraces which clotilda kept round his neck <\s>
<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>

<s> esmond's scheme his first visit was to bruxelles passing by way of antwerp where the duke of marlborough was in exile and in the first named place harry found his dear young benedict the married man who appeared to be rather out of humor with his matrimonial chain and clogged with the obstinate embraces which clotilda kept round his neck <\s>
<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>

<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>

<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>

<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>
<s> castlewood i have said was born in the same year as the prince of wales had not a little of the prince's air height and figure and especially since he had seen the chevalier de st <\s>
<s> george on the occasion before named took no small pride in his resemblance to a person so illustrious which likeness he increased by all means in his power wearing fair brown periwigs such as the prince wore and ribbons and so forth of the chevalier's color <\s>
<s> this resemblance was in truth the circumstance on which mr <\s>
<s> esmond's scheme was founded and having secured frank's secrecy and enthusiasm he left him to continue his journey and see the other personages on whom its success depended <\s>
<s> the place whither mr <\s>
<s> simon next travelled was bar in lorraine where that merchant arrived with a consignment of broadcloths valuable laces from malines and letters for his correspondent there <\s>
<s> would you know how a prince heroic from misfortunes and descended from a line of kings whose race seemed to be doomed like the atridae of old would you know how he was employed when the envoy who came to him through danger and difficulty beheld him for the first time <\s>
<s> the young king in a flannel jacket was at tennis with the gentlemen of his suite crying out after the balls and swearing like the meanest of his subjects <\s>
<s> the next time mr <\s>
<s> esmond saw him twas when monsieur simon took a packet of laces to miss oglethorpe the prince's ante chamber in those days at which ignoble door men were forced to knock for admission to his majesty <\s>
<s> the admission was given the envoy found the king and the mistress together the pair were at cards and his majesty was in liquor <\s>
<s> he cared more for three honors than three kingdoms and a half dozen glasses of ratafia made him forget all his woes and his losses his father's crown and his grandfather's head <\s>
<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>
<s> monsieur simon took his departure <\s>
<s> at any rate the youth at bar was as good as the older pretender at hanover if the worst came to the worst the englishman could be dealt with as easy as the german <\s>
<s> monsieur simon trotted on that long journey from nancy to paris and saw that famous town stealthily and like a spy as in truth he was and where sure more magnificence and more misery is heaped together more rags and lace more filth and gilding than in any city in this world <\s>
<s> here he was put in communication with the king's best friend his half brother the famous duke of berwick esmond recognized him as the stranger who had visited castlewood now near twenty years ago <\s>

<s> esmond was one of webb's brave regiment that had once been his grace's own <\s>

<s> never shake your head but hear me say you will hear me a year hence <\s>

<s> hear a last word <\s>
<s> i do love you <\s>
<s> i do admire you who would not that has known such love as yours has been for us all <\s>
<s> but i think i have no heart at least i have never seen the man that could touch it and had i found him i would have followed him in rags had he been a private soldier or to sea like one of those buccaneers you used to read to us about when we were children <\s>
<s> i would do anything for such a man bear anything for him but i never found one <\s>
<s> you were ever too much of a slave to win my heart even my lord duke could not command it <\s>
<s> i had not been happy had i married him <\s>
<s> i knew that three months after our engagement and was too vain to break it <\s>
<s> i cried once or twice not for him but with tears of rage because i could not be sorry for him <\s>
<s> i was frightened to find i was glad of his death and were i joined to you i should have the same sense of servitude the same longing to escape <\s>
<s> we should both be unhappy and you the most who are as jealous as the duke was himself <\s>
<s> i tried to love him i tried indeed i did affected gladness when he came submitted to hear when he was by me and tried the wife's part i thought i was to play for the rest of my days <\s>
<s> but half an hour of that complaisance wearied me and what would a lifetime be <\s>
<s> my thoughts were away when he was speaking and i was thinking oh that this man would drop my hand and rise up from before my feet <\s>
<s> i knew his great and noble qualities greater and nobler than mine a thousand times as yours are cousin i tell you a million and a million times better <\s>
<s> but twas not for these i took him <\s>
<s> i took him to have a great place in the world and i lost it <\s>
<s> i lost it and do not deplore him and i often thought as i listened to his fond vows and ardent words oh if i yield to this man and meet the other i shall hate him and leave him <\s>

<s> she is weak but she would die rather than do a wrong i am stronger than she but i would do it out of defiance <\s>

<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>

<s> esmond's scheme his first visit was to bruxelles passing by way of antwerp where the duke of marlborough was in exile and in the first named place harry found his dear young benedict the married man who appeared to be rather out of humor with his matrimonial chain and clogged with the obstinate embraces which clotilda kept round his neck <\s>
<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>

<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>

<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>

<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>

<s> esmond's scheme his first visit was to bruxelles passing by way of antwerp where the duke of marlborough was in exile and in the first named place harry found his dear young benedict the married man who appeared to be rather out of humor with his matrimonial chain and clogged with the obstinate embraces which clotilda kept round his neck <\s>
<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>

<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>

<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>
<s> monsieur simon took his departure <\s>

<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>

<s> esmond's scheme his first visit was to bruxelles passing by way of antwerp where the duke of marlborough was in exile and in the first named place harry found his dear young benedict the married man who appeared to be rather out of humor with his matrimonial chain and clogged with the obstinate embraces which clotilda kept round his neck <\s>
<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>

<s> esmond's scheme his first visit was to bruxelles passing by way of antwerp where the duke of marlborough was in exile and in the first named place harry found his dear young benedict the married man who appeared to be rather out of humor with his matrimonial chain and clogged with the obstinate embraces which clotilda kept round his neck <\s>
<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>
<s> castlewood i have said was born in the same year as the prince of wales had not a little of the prince's air height and figure and especially since he had seen the chevalier de st <\s>
<s> george on the occasion before named took no small pride in his resemblance to a person so illustrious which likeness he increased by all means in his power wearing fair brown periwigs such as the prince wore and ribbons and so forth of the chevalier's color <\s>
<s> this resemblance was in truth the circumstance on which mr <\s>

<s> the admission was given the envoy found the king and the mistress together the pair were at cards and his majesty was in liquor <\s>
<s> he cared more for three honors than three kingdoms and a half dozen glasses of ratafia made him forget all his woes and his losses his father's crown and his grandfather's head <\s>
<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>

<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>

<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>

<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>

<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>

<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>

<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>
<s> castlewood i have said was born in the same year as the prince of wales had not a little of the prince's air height and figure and especially since he had seen the chevalier de st <\s>
<s> george on the occasion before named took no small pride in his resemblance to a person so illustrious which likeness he increased by all means in his power wearing fair brown periwigs such as the prince wore and ribbons and so forth of the chevalier's color <\s>

<s> the admission was given the envoy found the king and the mistress together the pair were at cards and his majesty was in liquor <\s>
<s> he cared more for three honors than three kingdoms and a half dozen glasses of ratafia made him forget all his woes and his losses his father's crown and his grandfather's head <\s>
<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>
<s> monsieur simon took his departure <\s>
<s> at any rate the youth at bar was as good as the older pretender at hanover if the worst came to the worst the englishman could be dealt with as easy as the german <\s>

<s> esmond's scheme his first visit was to bruxelles passing by way of antwerp where the duke of marlborough was in exile and in the first named place harry found his dear young benedict the married man who appeared to be rather out of humor with his matrimonial chain and clogged with the obstinate embraces which clotilda kept round his neck <\s>
<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>

<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>

<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>

<s> esmond's scheme his first visit was to bruxelles passing by way of antwerp where the duke of marlborough was in exile and in the first named place harry found his dear young benedict the married man who appeared to be rather out of humor with his matrimonial chain and clogged with the obstinate embraces which clotilda kept round his neck <\s>
<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>
<s> castlewood i have said was born in the same year as the prince of wales had not a little of the prince's air height and figure and especially since he had seen the chevalier de st <\s>

<s> esmond's scheme his first visit was to bruxelles passing by way of antwerp where the duke of marlborough was in exile and in the first named place harry found his dear young benedict the married man who appeared to be rather out of humor with his matrimonial chain and clogged with the obstinate embraces which clotilda kept round his neck <\s>
<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>
<s> castlewood i have said was born in the same year as the prince of wales had not a little of the prince's air height and figure and especially since he had seen the chevalier de st <\s>
<s> george on the occasion before named took no small pride in his resemblance to a person so illustrious which likeness he increased by all means in his power wearing fair brown periwigs such as the prince wore and ribbons and so forth of the chevalier's color <\s>
<s> this resemblance was in truth the circumstance on which mr <\s>

<s> the admission was given the envoy found the king and the mistress together the pair were at cards and his majesty was in liquor <\s>
<s> he cared more for three honors than three kingdoms and a half dozen glasses of ratafia made him forget all his woes and his losses his father's crown and his grandfather's head <\s>
<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>

<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>

<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>

<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>

<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>

<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>

<s> colonel esmond was not presented to her but monsieur simon was a gentleman of the royal cravat esmond bethought him of the regiment of his honest irishman whom he had seen that day after malplaquet when he first set eyes on the young king ); and monsieur simon was introduced to the viscountess castlewood nee comptesse wertheim to the numerous counts the lady clotilda's tall brothers to her father the chamberlain and to the lady his wife frank's mother in law a tall and majestic person of large proportions such as became the mother of such a company of grenadiers as her warlike sons formed <\s>
<s> the whole race were at free quarters in the little castle nigh to bruxelles which frank had taken rode his horses drank his wine and lived easily at the poor lad's charges <\s>
<s> esmond had always maintained a perfect fluency in the french which was his mother tongue and if this family that spoke french with the twang which the flemings use discovered any inaccuracy in mr <\s>
<s> simon's pronunciation twas to be attributed to the latter's long residence in england where he had married and remained ever since he was taken prisoner at blenheim <\s>
<s> his story was perfectly pat there were none there to doubt it save honest frank and he was charmed with his kinsman's scheme when he became acquainted with it and in truth always admired colonel esmond with an affectionate fidelity and thought his cousin the wisest and best of all cousins and men <\s>
<s> frank entered heart and soul into the plan and liked it the better as it was to take him to paris out of reach of his brothers his father and his mother in law whose attentions rather fatigued him <\s>
<s> castlewood i have said was born in the same year as the prince of wales had not a little of the prince's air height and figure and especially since he had seen the chevalier de st <\s>
<s> george on the occasion before named took no small pride in his resemblance to a person so illustrious which likeness he increased by all means in his power wearing fair brown periwigs such as the prince wore and ribbons and so forth of the chevalier's color <\s>
<s> this resemblance was in truth the circumstance on which mr <\s>
<s> esmond's scheme was founded and having secured frank's secrecy and enthusiasm he left him to continue his journey and see the other personages on whom its success depended <\s>

<s> the admission was given the envoy found the king and the mistress together the pair were at cards and his majesty was in liquor <\s>
<s> he cared more for three honors than three kingdoms and a half dozen glasses of ratafia made him forget all his woes and his losses his father's crown and his grandfather's head <\s>
<s> esmond did not open himself to the prince then <\s>
<s> his majesty was scarce in a condition to hear him and he doubted whether a king who drank so much could keep a secret in his fuddled head or whether a hand that shook so was strong enough to grasp at a crown <\s>
<s> however at last and after taking counsel with the prince's advisers amongst whom were many gentlemen honest and faithful esmond's plan was laid before the king and her actual majesty queen oglethorpe in council <\s>
<s> the prince liked the scheme well enough twas easy and daring and suited to his reckless gayety and lively youthful spirit <\s>
<s> in the morning after he had slept his wine off he was very gay lively and agreeable <\s>
<s> his manner had an extreme charm of archness and a kind simplicity and to do her justice her oglethorpean majesty was kind acute resolute and of good counsel she gave the prince much good advice that he was too weak to follow and loved him with a fidelity which he returned with an ingratitude quite royal <\s>
<s> having his own forebodings regarding his scheme should it ever be fulfilled and his usual sceptic doubts as to the benefit which might accrue to the country by bringing a tipsy young monarch back to it colonel esmond had his audience of leave and quiet <\s>
<s> monsieur simon took his departure <\s>
<s> at any rate the youth at bar was as good as the older pretender at hanover if the worst came to the worst the englishman could be dealt with as easy as the german <\s>
<s> monsieur simon trotted on that long journey from nancy to paris and saw that famous town stealthily and like a spy as in truth he was and where sure more magnificence and more misery is heaped together more rags and lace more filth and gilding than in any city in this world <\s>
<s> here he was put in communication with the king's best friend his half brother the famous duke of berwick esmond recognized him as the stranger who had visited castlewood now near twenty years ago <\s>

<s> esmond was one of webb's brave regiment that had once been his grace's own <\s>

<s> had berwick been his father's heir james the third had assuredly sat on the english throne <\s>
<s> he could dare endure strike speak be silent <\s>
<s> the fire and genius perhaps he had not that were given to baser men but except these he had some of the best qualities of a leader <\s>

<s> but esmond did not choose to enter on it nor did the duke press him <\s>
<s> you will give them to your wife cousin says she <\s>
<s> my cousin your wife has a lovely complexion and shape <\s>
<s> beatrix esmond burst out the old fire flaming out as it would at times will you wear those trinkets at your marriage <\s>
<s> you whispered once you did not know me you know me better now how i sought what i have sighed for for ten years what foregone <\s>
<s> a price for your constancy my lord <\s>
<s> says she such a preux chevalier wants to be paid <\s>
<s> again esmond spoke out if i do something you have at heart something worthy of me and you something that shall make me a name with which to endow you will you take it <\s>
<s> there was a chance for me once you said is it impossible to recall it <\s>
<s> never shake your head but hear me say you will hear me a year hence <\s>
<s> if i come back to you and bring you fame will that please you <\s>
<s> if i do what you desire most what he who is dead desired most will that soften you <\s>
<s> what is it henry <\s>
<s> says she her face lighting up what mean you <\s>
<s> ask no questions he said wait and give me but time if i bring back that you long for that i have a thousand times heard you pray for will you have no reward for him who has done you that service <\s>
<s> put away those trinkets keep them it shall not be at my marriage it shall not be at yours but if man can do it i swear a day shall come when there shall be a feast in your house and you shall be proud to wear them <\s>
<s> i say no more now put aside these words and lock away yonder box until the day when i shall remind you of both <\s>
<s> all i pray of you now is to wait and to remember <\s>
<s> you are going out of the country <\s>
<s> says beatrix in some agitation <\s>
<s> yes to morrow says esmond <\s>
<s> says beatrix laying her hand on his arm twas the hand on which she wore the duke's bracelet <\s>
<s> continued she with a tone that had more despondency in it than she was accustomed to show <\s>
<s> hear a last word <\s>
<s> i do love you <\s>
<s> i do admire you who would not that has known such love as yours has been for us all <\s>
<s> but i think i have no heart at least i have never seen the man that could touch it and had i found him i would have followed him in rags had he been a private soldier or to sea like one of those buccaneers you used to read to us about when we were children <\s>
<s> i would do anything for such a man bear anything for him but i never found one <\s>
<s> you were ever too much of a slave to win my heart even my lord duke could not command it <\s>
<s> i had not been happy had i married him <\s>
<s> i knew that three months after our engagement and was too vain to break it <\s>
<s> i cried once or twice not for him but with tears of rage because i could not be sorry for him <\s>
<s> i was frightened to find i was glad of his death and were i joined to you i should have the same sense of servitude the same longing to escape <\s>
<s> we should both be unhappy and you the most who are as jealous as the duke was himself <\s>
<s> i tried to love him i tried indeed i did affected gladness when he came submitted to hear when he was by me and tried the wife's part i thought i was to play for the rest of my days <\s>
<s> but half an hour of that complaisance wearied me and what would a lifetime be <\s>
<s> my thoughts were away when he was speaking and i was thinking oh that this man would drop my hand and rise up from before my feet <\s>
<s> i knew his great and noble qualities greater and nobler than mine a thousand times as yours are cousin i tell you a million and a million times better <\s>
<s> but twas not for these i took him <\s>
<s> i took him to have a great place in the world and i lost it <\s>
<s> i lost it and do not deplore him and i often thought as i listened to his fond vows and ardent words oh if i yield to this man and meet the other i shall hate him and leave him <\s>
<s> i am not good harry my mother is gentle and good like an angel <\s>
<s> i wonder how she should have had such a child <\s>
<s> she is weak but she would die rather than do a wrong i am stronger than she but i would do it out of defiance <\s>
<s> i do not care for what the parsons tell me with their droning sermons i used to see them at court as mean and as worthless as the meanest woman there <\s>
<s> oh i am sick and weary of the world <\s>
<s> i wait but for one thing and when tis done i will take frank's religion and your poor mother's and go into a nunnery and end like her <\s>
<s> shall i wear the diamonds then they say the nuns wear their best trinkets the day they take the veil <\s>
<s> i will put them away as you bid me farewell cousin mamma is pacing the next room racking her little head to know what we have been saying <\s>
<s> she is jealous all women are <\s>
<s> i sometimes think that is the only womanly quality i have <\s>
<s> she gave him her cheek as a brotherly privilege <\s>
<s> the cheek was as cold as marble <\s>
<s> esmond's mistress showed no signs of jealousy when he returned to the room where she was <\s>
<s> she had schooled herself so as to look quite inscrutably when she had a mind <\s>
<s> amongst her other feminine qualities she had that of being a perfect dissembler <\s>
<s> he rode away from castlewood to attempt the task he was bound on and stand or fall by it in truth his state of mind was such that he was eager for some outward excitement to counteract that gnawing malady which he was inwardly enduring <\s>
<s> i travel to france and bring home a portrait of rigaud <\s>
<s> esmond did not think fit to take leave at court or to inform all the world of pall mall and the coffee houses that he was about to quit england and chose to depart in the most private manner possible <\s>
